<leme no="489">
<page sig="a1r">
<section type="title-page">
 
A
<f type="rl">PHYSICAL</f>
Dictionary:
OR,
An Interpretation of such crabbed
Words and Terms of Arts, as are deriv'd
from the Greek or Latin, and used in <f type="i">Phy&shy;
sick</f>, <f type="i">Anatomy</f>, <f type="i">Chirurgery</f>, and <f type="i">Chymistry</f>.
With a definition of most Diseases incident
to the Body of Man; and a description of 
the Marks and Characters used by Doctors
in their Receipts.

This Dictionary will be as useful and suffici&shy;
ent to all our late English Practitioners in
Physics or Chirurgery (especially such as
are not Scholars) as any Dictionary of
Ten Shillings Price.

Approved by several Doctors, Surgeons and
Apothecaries: And Recommended by
them in an Epistle to all English Practitio&shy;
ners in Physick and Chirurgery.

<f type="i">London</f>. Printed by <f type="i">G. D.</f> for <f type="i">John Garfield</f>,
and are to be sold at his Shop at the sign of the 
<f type="i">Rolling-Press for Pictures</f>, near the Royal
Exchange in Corn-hil, over against
Popes head-alley. 1657.
</section>
</page>

<page sig="a1v">
</page>

<page sig="a2r">
<section type="practitioners epistle">
To all English Pra&shy;
ctitioners in <f type="i">Phy&shy;
sick</f>, <f type="i">Anatomy</f>, <f type="i">Chi&shy;
rurgery</f>, and <f type="i">Chy&shy;
mistry</f>.

H<f type="i">Ow great the
necessity is,
of having a 
</f>PHYSICALL
DICTIONARY <f type="i">for ex&shy;
plaining hard Words
</page>

<page sig="a2v">
and terms of Art in the 
Medicinal Sciences
of</f> Physick, Chyrur&shy;
gery, <f type="i">and</f> Chymistry,
<f type="i">such as are vers'd in
the understanding those
most useful, mysterious
and noble Arts, do
very well know: It is
intended for such Per&shy;
sons as spend their 
time and employment
in studying Physick,
and are acquainted 
with no other than
</page>

<page sig="a3r">
their Mother tongue;
yet, many times more
readily Cure a Disease,
by their observant, dili&shy;
gent, and strict keeping
to an approved Me&shy;
dicine, than many o&shy;
thers, that trust wholly
to their Art: There&shy;
fore, for the help of
charitable and honest&shy;
meaning People, this</f>
Dictionary <f type="i">was Com&shy;
piled, which hath in it
as much as is necessary
</page>

<page sig="a3v">
for understanding hard
Words in the fore&shy;
mentioned Arts, be&shy;
ing freed from that
troublesome and su&shy;
perfluous Number of
unnecessary Words
which serve for no&shy;
thing but to swell up
the Bulk and Price
of Books.

And thus much we
have thought fit,
(English Reader)
to say unto thee in
</page>

<page sig="a4r">
Commendation of this
best of Physical Dictio&shy;
naries.</f>

George Starky, <f type="i">Doctor of Physick.</f>
George Thornley, <f type="i">Doctor of Physick.</f>
Thomas Herbert, <f type="i">Student in Physick
and Astrologie.</f>
John Rowland, <f type="i">Doctor of Physick.</f>
John Hawkins, <f type="i">Chirurgion.</f>
John Roane,  <f type="i">Chirurgion.</f>
John Beach, <f type="i">Student in Physick
and Surgery.</f>
Philip Frith, <f type="i">Student in Physick
and Astrology.</f>
Ralph Woodall,  <f type="i">Chirurgion.</f>
John Bryan, <f type="i">Student in Physick.</f>
Anthony Rowe,  <f type="i">Chirurgion.</f>
John North, <f type="i">Apothecary.</f>
John Straw, <f type="i">Practitioner in Physick.</f>
John Harvey, <f type="i">Apothecary.</f>
</section>
</page>

<page sig="a4v">
</page>

<page sig="a5r">
<section type="stationer's epistle">
THE
STATIONER
TO HIS
COUNTRY-MEN.

Kind Countrimen,

T<f type="i">He Explaining
the Art of</f>
Physick, <f type="i">ha&shy;
ving found so
welcome En&shy;
tertainment, I hope for the like
friendly acceptance amongst you,
having preserved this</f> Dictio&shy;
nary <f type="i">for your Good, which o&shy;
</page>

<page sig="a5v">
thers would have depriv'd you
of, wherein such difficult terms
as are deriv'd from the Greek or
Latin, and dark to the English
Reader, are made English; and
such Marks and Characters as
are used by Physitians and Apo&shy;
thecaries in their Receipts ex&shy;
plained; and for your ease and
better understanding, put down
the signification of their Weights
and Measures according to their
Characters: with a definition 
of most Diseases incident to the
body of man. And whereas
there are many Words in Mr.</f>
Tomlinson<f type="i">'s Translation of</f>
Rh&aelig;nod&aelig;us Dispensatory,
<f type="i">not understood by any ordinary
</page>

<page sig="A6r">
Scholars (much less such as are
not) I have caused them to be
explained by able persons, well
acquainted with the</f> Practice
of Physick, <f type="i">so that the mean&shy;
est Capacity, by making use
thereof, may rightly understand
whatever difficult expressions he
shall meet withal in the said
Dispensatory.</f>

Your Friend, and Servant,

<f type="i">Joh. Garfield.</f>
</section>
</page>

land:  This juyce is somewhat

pleasant taste:  being dropt into
